## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: materials science / constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, a core problem in solid mechanics and materials science. Stress typically increases with strain (via elastic modulus or strain hardening) and decreases with increasing temperature due to thermal softening.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic regime, small strains)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - c2 * T) (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic strain hardening, Hollomon equation)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with yield stress offset)
- Johnson-Cook strength model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook with homologous temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - (c3 * T)**c4) (power-law thermal softening)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(-c2 * epsilon) (saturation hardening model)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(-c2 * epsilon)) * exp(-c3 * T) (saturation hardening with Arrhenius-type softening)
- Arrhenius-type flow stress: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 / T) * epsilon**c2 (thermally activated deformation)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(-c2 * T) (power-law hardening with exponential thermal decay)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse form: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (combined linear and nonlinear strain terms)
- Swift hardening with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * (c3 - c4 * T) (shifted power law with thermal softening)
- Hyperbolic sine flow rule: sigma = c0 * T * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 / T)) (Garofalo/Sellars-Tegart creep model inverted)
- Polynomial with temperature coupling: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon * T + c2 * epsilon**2 (quadratic expansion in strain and temperature)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening saturation → Use (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or tanh(c*epsilon) to capture stress plateau at large strains
- Linear thermal softening → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (Tm - T) representing distance from melting temperature
- Thermally activated processes → Arrhenius factor exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) capturing diffusion-controlled deformation
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 representing initial yield strength before hardening begins
- Separable strain-temperature structure → Product form f(epsilon) * g(T) reflecting independent hardening and softening mechanisms
- Shifted power law for pre-strain → (epsilon + c0)**c1 instead of epsilon**c1 to avoid singularity at zero strain
- Modulus degradation with temperature → Elastic slope c0*(1 - c1*T) or c0*exp(-c1*T) reflecting bond weakening
- Strain-temperature coupling → Terms like epsilon*T or epsilon**c1 * T**c2 representing dynamic strain aging or other coupled phenomena
